np.ndarray[ndim=2]\n        orig_values = values\n\n        dtype = values.dtype\n        is_numeric = dtype.kind in \"iufcb\"\n\n        is_datetimelike = dtype.kind in \"mM\"\n\n        if self.how in [\"any\", \"all\"]:\n            if mask is None:\n                mask = isna(values)\n\n        if is_datetimelike:\n            values = values.view(\"int64\")\n            is_numeric = True\n        elif dtype.kind == \"b\":\n            values = values.view(\"uint8\")\n        if values.dtype == \"float16\":\n            values = values.astype(np.float32)\n\n        if self.how in [\"any\", \"all\"]:\n            if dtype == object:\n                if kwargs[\"skipna\"]:\n                    # TODO: min_count\n            if self.how != \"rank\":\n                # TODO: should rank take result_mask?\n                kwargs[\"result_mask\"] = result_mask\n            func(\n                out=result,\n                values=values,\n                labels=comp_ids,\n                ngroups=ngroups,\n                is_datetimelike=is_datetimelike,\n                mask=mask,\n                **kwargs,\n            )\n\n        if self.kind == \"aggregate\" and self.how not in [\"idxmin\", \"idxmax\"]:\n            # i.e. counts is defined.  Locations where count<min_count\n            # need to have the result set to np.nan, which may require casting,\n            # see GH#40767. For idxmin/idxmax is handled specially via post-processing\n            if result.dtype.kind in \"iu\" and not is_datetimelike:\n                # if the op keeps the int dtypes, we have to use 0\n                cutoff = max(0 if self.how in [\"sum\", \"prod\"] else 1, min_count)\n                empty_groups = counts < cutoff\n                if empty_groups.any():\n                    if result_mask is not None:\n                        assert result_mask[empty_groups].all()\n                    else:\n                        # Note: this conversion could be lossy, see GH#40767\n                        result = result.astype(\"float64\")\n                        result[empty_groups] = np.nan\n\n        result = result.T\n\n        if self.how not in self.cast_blocklist:\n            # e.g. if we are int64 and need to restore to datetime64/timedelta64\n            # \"rank\" is the only member of cast_blocklist we get here\n            # Casting only needed for float16, bool, datetimelike,\n            #  and self.how in [\"sum\", \"prod\", \"ohlc\", \"cumprod\"]\n            res_dtype = self._get_result_dtype(orig_values.dtype)\n            op_result = maybe_downcast_to_dtype(result, res_dtype)\n        else:\n            op_result = result\n\n        return op_result\n\n    @final\n    def _validate_axis(self, axis: AxisInt, values: ArrayLike) -> @final\n    def _get_splitter(self, data: NDFrame) -> DataSplitter:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns\n        -------\n        Generator yielding subsetted objects\n        \"\"\"\n        if @cache_readonly\n    def result_ilocs(self) -> npt.NDArray[np.intp]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Get the original integer locations of result_index in the input.\n        \"\"\"\n        # Original ids = self.ids\n\n        if self.has_dropped_na:\n            mask = np.where(ids >= 0)\n            # Count how many gaps are caused by previous null values for each position\n            null_gaps = np.cumsum(ids == -1)[mask]\n            ids = ids[mask]\n\n        result = get_group_index_sorter(ids, self.ngroups)\n\n        if self.has_dropped_na:\n            # Shift by the number of prior unobserved and observed parts\n            names = self.names\n            codes = [ping.codes for ping in self.groupings]\n            ob_indices = [idx for idx, ob in enumerate(obs) if ob]\n ) -> npt.NDArray[np.object_]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Faster aggregation using direct label indexing instead of creating sorted groups.\n        Avoids the overhead of DataSplitter sorting and Series object creation.\n        \"\"\"\n        result = np.empty(self.ngroups, dtype=\"O\")\n        initialized = False\n        ids = self.ids\n\n        # Accumulate indices for each group label\n        group_indices: dict[int, list[int]] = {}\n        for label_id in range(self.ngroups):\n            group_indices[label_id] = []\n\n        # Collect indices for each group (skip NA labels)\n        for i, label_id in enumerate(ids):\n            if label_id >= 0:\n                group_indices[label_id].append(i)\n\n        # Apply function to each group\n        for label_id in range(self.ngroups):\n            indices = group_indices[label_id]\n            if indices:\n                # Use iloc to create group without sorting/copying\n                group = obj.iloc[indices]\n            else:\n                # Empty group - create empty Series with same dtype\n                group = obj.iloc[:0]\n\n            res = func(group)\n            res = initialized = True\n\n            result[label_id] = res\n\n        return result\n\n    @final\n    def apply_groupwise(\n        self, f: Callable, data: DataFrame | Series\n    ) -> tuple[list, bool]:\n        mutated = False\n        splitter = self._get_splitter(data)\n        group_keys = self.result_index\n        result_values = []\n\n        # This calls DataSplitter.__iter__\n        zipped = zip(group_keys, splitter, strict=True)\n\n        for key, group in zipped:\n            # Pinning name is needed for\n            #  test_group_apply_once_per_group,\n            #  test_inconsistent_return_type, test_set_group_name,\n            #  test_group_name_available_in_inference_pass,\n            #  test_groupby_multi_timezone\n            object.__setattr__(group, \"name\", key)\n\n            # group might be modified\n            group_axes = group.axes\n            res = f(group)\n            if not mutated and not _is_indexed_like(res, group_axes):\n                mutated = True\n            result_values.append(res)\n        # getattr pattern for __name__ is needed for functools.partial objects\n        if len(group_keys) == 0 and getattr(f, \"__name__\", None) in [\n            \"skew\",\n            \"kurt\",\n            \"sum\",\n            \"prod\",\n        ]:\n            #  If group_keys is empty, then no function calls have been result = result[result >= 0]\n        return result\n\n\nclass BinGrouper(BaseGrouper):\n    \"\"\"\n    This is an internal Grouper class\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    bins : the split index
